Technical Memorandum
To:     John Karachepone, PE (G&O)
From: H. Roger Sharp, PE (G&A)
Date:   12/7/2004
Re:     Job# 2654.02 Traffic Analysis for Intersection of Beach Boulevard and University Boulevard,
        Jacksonville, FL


Ghyabi & Associates, Inc. (G&A) has been retained by Greenhorn & O'Mara, Inc. (G&O) to provide
future design traffic projections for proposed intersection improvements at Beach Boulevard and
University Boulevard in Jacksonville, Florida.

This technical memorandum presents the initial traffic information for this project. Included within
this document are the observed 2004 Annual Average Daily Traffic (AADT), design hour factors (K,
D, and T), proposed future year AADT and initial design hour turning movements for the primary
intersections within the study area. The project's location is shown graphically in Figure 1.

Data Collection
This technical memorandum documents the traffic data collected to conduct the study and includes an
analysis of the existing conditions. Traffic count data for this study were collected by G&A.

Traffic counts:
To determine the overall traffic volumes on the main roadways, 3-day vehicle bi-directional classified
machine counts were taken at the following locations:
        A.    Beach Boulevard west of University Boulevard
        B.    Beach Boulevard east of University Boulevard
        C.    University Boulevard north of Beach Boulevard
        D.    University Boulevard south of Beach Boulevard
        E.    Coronet Lane west of University Boulevard
        F.    Booth Road west of University Boulevard

The vehicles that were counted were classified into 13 vehicle types, which were subsequently
grouped into three primary vehicle types:

              Passenger Vehicles - motorcycle, cars, vans, and pickup trucks;
              Medium Trucks ­ buses and single unit trucks;
              Heavy Trucks ­ (3 or 4 axles) single unit trucks, 2-axle tractors (with 1 or 2 axles
              trailers), 3-axle tractors (with 2 or 3 axle trailers), and (5, 6, and 7-axle) multi-trailers.

Using these categories, the overall percentage of trucks (medium and heavy) was determined for peak
and daily traffic conditions.

In order to determine the turning movements at the main intersection of Beach Blvd. and University
Blvd., together with the turning movements at other intersections and major driveways 4-hour manual
turning movement counts were conducted over two days at the following locations:

        1.       Beach Blvd. @ Albertsons East Entrance
        2.       Beach Blvd. @ Albertsons West Entrance
        3.       Beach Blvd. @ Brooks Hospital East Entrance

        6.       Beach Blvd. @ Hickman Road
        7.       Beach Blvd. @ Kmart & Staples East
        8.       Beach Blvd. @ Kmart & Staples West
        9.       Beach Blvd. @ Ryan Road
        10.      Beach Blvd. @ Southtrust Bank Entrance
        11.      Beach Blvd. @ Ten Broeck Hospital East
        12.      Beach Blvd. @ Ten Broeck Hospital West
        13.      Beach Blvd. @ University Blvd.
        14.      Beach Blvd. @ Walgreens Entrance

        16.      University Blvd. @ Booth Road
        17.      University Blvd. @ Brooks Hospital
        18.      University Blvd. @ Cruz Road
        19.      University Blvd. @ Hickson Road

        21.      University Blvd. @ Lottie Street

    Figure 2 shows the approximate location and type of each traffic count conducted for this study.
    Based on 72-hour approach classification counts, peak to daily factors (K) and the peak-hour peak-
    direction factors (D) were obtained. Table 1 shows the 24-hour, traffic count volumes, and analyses
    which include the measured K, D, daily and peak-hour truck percentages.

    Figures 3, 4, and 5 show the AM peak-hour, PM peak-hour, and existing geometry, respectively.
    Based on the volume counts, the morning peak-hour was found to be from 7:15am to 8:15am, and the
    evening peak-hour was from 4:45pm to 5:45pm. The raw traffic count data are provided as an
    attachment.

                                        Table 1: Traffic Count Summary
                                                      Daily                               Peak Hour
  Roadway             Location        ADT       T      Direction     K   Volume      Start Finish     D       T
University Blvd.   S of Beach        35,169   4.50%   Southbound   0.073   2,584       7:45   8:45 59.20%   4.90%
University Blvd.   N of Beach        32,933   5.00%   Southbound   0.070   2,308       7:15   8:15 57.10%   4.40%
Beach Blvd.        W of University   34,136   4.30%   Westbound    0.072   2,446       7:45   8:45 54.30%   4.50%
Beach Blvd.        E of University   35,306   4.20%   Eastbound    0.071   2,522      12:15 13:15 50.90%    4.60%

    Other traffic count information:
    In addition to the field traffic count data collection, traffic count information from FDOT and Duval
    County were also used for this analysis. Information from these data sources was used in combination
    with the field traffic count data to develop design factors such as K, D, and T. Table 2 shows the
    relevant information obtained from the FDOT 2000 Florida Traffic Information CD.

Design Characteristics
Traffic design characteristics for the project were developed from the traffic count data collected in
the field and from FDOT traffic count information. These design characteristics include design hour
traffic flow factor (K30=9.44%), directional distribution factor (D=53.54%), and daily truck factor
(Tdaily=3.99%). Table 1 shows the K, D and T factors obtained from the traffic counts. The observed K
factor varies from 7.0% on University Blvd. north of Beach Blvd. to 7.3% on University Blvd. south
of Beach Blvd. These values for K are low and reflect the congested conditions at the intersection.
The more conservative K factor of 9.44 obtained from the FDOT database, which is based on a larger
sample, is recommended for this analysis.

The D factors obtained from the counts on Beach Blvd.: 50.9% east of University Blvd. and 54.3%
west of University Blvd. give an average of 52.6%. This is slightly less than the FDOT value of
9.44%. On University Blvd, the observed D factors are 59.2% and 57.1% south, and north of Beach
Blvd. respectively. It is recommended that the average of these two values, i.e. 58.15% be used for
University Blvd.

Additionally, to be conservative, the higher truck percentage, obtained from the counts is
recommended for this project. Table 3 provides the recommended K30, D, T factors proposed for the
initial use of the project.

                          Table 3: Recommended Design Characteristics
                                 Roadway            K30       D         T
                             Beach Boulevard        9.44    53.54     4.25%
                           University Boulevard     9.44    58.15     4.75%

Future Travel Demand
The development of the traffic projections for the corridor requires the examination of historical
traffic growth, proposed development within the corridor vicinity, a basic understanding of the traffic
circulation patterns and relevant characteristics of the corridor.

Trend Analysis
FDOT historical traffic count information was collected for the following FDOT count stations:
                  FDOT Count Station 0942 ­ SR 212 (Beach Boulevard) ­ 100' west of SR115
                  FDOT Count Station 3822 ­ SR 115 (University Boulevard) ­ 0.6 mi. south of SR 212
                  FDOT Count Station 3623 ­ SR 212 (Beach Boulevard) ­ 50' east of Service Road

A linear regression or trend analysis was performed at each location to determine past growth and
projected traffic growth for each specific location. Table 4 shows a summary of the trend-projected
growth. The table shows growth rates based on historical traffic growth and projected 2025 traffic
volumes using the trend line. It should be noted that future travel demand estimated from trends
analyses are based on historical traffic and the growth in economic development in the study area
under the existing roadway system. The future travel demand projections, based on a trend analysis,
do not take into account roadway improvements within the study area.

It should be noted that as shown in Table 4, the R2 values are too low for the regression analysis to be

caution.
Florida Standard Urban Transportation Model System (FSUTMS)
The First Coast MPO provided the currently adopted Jacksonville Urban Area Transportation
Structure (JUATS) model. The MPO maintains models for the 1998 validation year, 2005, 2015, and
2025. The modeling efforts were representative of the latest available socio-economic input data,
which were available at the time of this report.
Mr. John Karachepone P.E. (G&O)
December 7, 2004
Page 19

Utilizing the output from the FSUTMS network, travel demand forecasts for the base year 1998 were
compared to the 1998 traffic counts. As shown in Table 5, the model over assigns traffic to University
Boulevard north of Beach Boulevard and under assigns traffic on the other three approaches.
However, the model assignment is within the acceptable deviation on all approaches. The screenline
model volume in the north-south screenline is accurate within -0.05 percent (1998 count of 84,832 vs.
model volume of 80,503). Since the overall magnitude of the project volumes appears reasonable, no
network coding changes were made. Volume plots for the base year (1998) and future year (2025) are
included as attachments.

                                      Table 5: Model Assignments
      Location                                  1998  1998 Model         Deviation      Maximum
                                               Counts Assignment                        Desirable
                                                                                        Deviation*
      University Blvd, North of Beach Blvd      35,500          46,059        29.74%       24%

      University Blvd, South of Beach Blvd      41,500          34,355    -17.22%          22%

      Beach Blvd, West of University Blvd       33,000          33,331        1.00%        24%

      Beach Blvd, East of University Blvd       33,500          34,818        3.93%        24%
* Source: NCHRP 255, page 41, December 1981.

2025.

                             Table 6: Unadjusted Model Growth Rate
                                                    1998               2025
                                             Number         Number                 Growth
           Roadway                           of Lanes Model of Lanes Model          Rate

On Beach Boulevard, the model projected 0.5% average annual growth rate west of University
Boulevard and ­0.2% east of University Boulevard. South of Beach Boulevard, the model is
projecting zero growth and ­0.9% north of Beach Boulevard. The model results are consistent with
the projections made from the historical traffic counts. Although negative growth rates are counter
intuitive, they are reflective of the stable, unchanging nature of the development in the vicinity and
the congested conditions. In reality, drivers will adjust their driving pattern according to the actual
traffic conditions on the roadways. There are no major roadways running parallel to University
Boulevard, and although neighborhood streets do provide some relief, the impact is small. Some of
the traffic projected by the model to use Beach Boulevard may use the Hart Expressway, but this is
not a parallel facility.
Mr. John Karachepone P.E. (G&O)
December 7, 2004
Page 20


Recommended Growth Rates
The trends analyses show a poor correlation between the traffic volumes and the passage of time at all
the reported count stations. The R2 values vary from 3.91% to 33.72%. However, the growth rate
trend does not account for future planned roadway improvements on parallel facilities that may
possibly decrease the traffic volumes on Beach Boulevard and University Boulevard or increases that
may occur from increasing car ownership and possible intensification of the commercial activity near
the intersection. The traffic projections based on both historical counts and in modeling are showing a
reduction in traffic, except west of University Boulevard on Beach Boulevard, where both
methodologies show a slight positive growth (Historical count projections show 0.74% and the model
shows 0.05% growth.) Therefore, since a negative growth rate is unrealistic, it was assumed that
growth on Beach Boulevard would be 1.00% and on University Boulevard it would be 0.05%. Figure
6 graphically illustrates the future AADT's and DDHV's, respectively.

                               Table 7: Recommended Growth Rates

                          Roadway                           Growth Rate
                          Beach Boulevard
                          West of University Blvd.               1.0%
                          East of University Blvd.               0.5%
                          University Boulevard
                          North of Beach Blvd.                   0.5%
                          South of Beach Blvd.                   0.5%


Design Traffic Forecasts
Application of the recommended growth rates to the existing volume (year 2004) produces future
year forecasts. Figure 6 graphically illustrates the future AADT and DDHV. Using the future traffic
volumes and recommended design characteristics, directional design hourly volumes (DDHV's) were
developed. The future AM and PM peak-hours turning movement volumes at the intersection were
projected using the FDOT spreadsheet TURNS 5. The inputs to the spreadsheet consist of the existing
turning movement counts, the existing AADT's, and the proposed growth rates. It should be noted
that the results represent the existing and future DDHV volumes at the intersections. The volumes are
calculated by the application of the proposed K30 and D factor to the AADT to forecast the future
turning movement volumes, which may be different from the K and D factors observed at the AM and
PM peak-hours. In addition, the distribution of the future turning movement at the intersection after
improvements may be different from the distribution of existing turning movement counts. Figures 7
and 8 present the turning movement volumes at the intersection of Beach Boulevard and University
Boulevard for the AM and PM peak-hour, respectively.

The AADT and DDHV values for the roadway segments are shown in Table 8. The AADT was
obtained by applying the appropriate value obtained from the FDOT 2003 Peak Season Factor
Category Report. The values for DDHV were calculated using the recommended growth factors and
K and D factors.
